4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# GCC Stack Clash Protection Implementation Audit

## Your Task

Audit the stack clash protection implementation in GCC. Find all C/C++ source files in `gcc-mirror/gcc` that implement stack clash mitigation. Specifically: 1. The file that implements stack clash probing for x86_64 targets (`gcc/config/i386/i386.cc` — look for `stack_clash_protection`). 2. The file that implements the generic stack clash expansion (`gcc/explow.cc` — look for `anti_adjust_stack_and_probe`). 3. The header where `TARGET_STACK_CLASH_PROTECTION` is declared or defined. 4. The test file under `gcc/testsuite/gcc.target/i386/` that validates stack clash protection (look for `stack-clash-*`). 5. The common options file where `-fstack-clash-protection` is defined (`gcc/common.opt`). Report each file path and the key function or definition.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

95-assistanttext-
I've completed a comprehensive audit of the GCC stack clash protection implementation. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've identified all the key files implementing stack clash protection in GCC and documented them in `/workspace/answer.json`:

### **Core Components:**

1. **Generic Stack Clash Implementation** (`gcc/explow.cc`):
   - `compute_stack_clash_protection_loop_data()` - Calculates probing parameters
   - `anti_adjust_stack_and_probe_stack_clash()` - Main expansion function
   - `emit_stack_clash_protection_probe_loop_start/end()` - Loop generation

2. **x86_64/i386 Target-Specific** (`gcc/config/i386/`):
   - `i386.md` - Machine description with `allocate_stack` patterns
   - `i386.cc` - Core backend implementation
   - `i386-protos.h` - Declares `ix86_target_stack_probe()`

3. **Target Hook Definition** (`gcc/target.def`):
   - `TARGET_STACK_CLASH_PROTECTION_ALLOCA_PROBE_RANGE` - Allows per-target customization

4. **Default Implementation** (`gcc/targhooks.cc`):
   - `default_stack_clash_protection_alloca_probe_range()` - Generic fallback

5. **Compiler Options**:
   - `gcc/common.opt` - `-fstack-clash-protection` flag
   - `gcc/params.opt` - Guard size and probe interval parameters

6. **Test Suite** (`gcc/testsuite/gcc.target/i386/`):
   - `stack-clash-protection.c` - Main validation test
   - `stack-check-11.c`, `stack-check-12.c`, `stack-check-17.c`, `stack-check-18.c`, `stack-check-19.c` - Specific test cases

The implementation follows a clear architecture: generic expansion code in `explow.cc` is called by target-specific patterns in `i386.md`, with optional customization via target hooks in `target.def`.

This file contains four critical functions:\\n\\n- **`compute_stack_clash_protection_loop_data()`** (line 1955): Computes parameters for the stack clash probing loop, including rounded allocation size, last address, residual size, and probe interval. It handles both:\\n  - Small allocations: Probes inline with simple interval-based probes\\n  - Large allocations: Uses loop-based probing with `emit_stack_clash_protection_probe_loop_start()` and `emit_stack_clash_protection_probe_loop_end()`\\n  - Residual allocations: Additional probing for non-aligned remainder\\n\\n- **`emit_stack_clash_protection_probe_loop_start()`** (line 2014): Emits the initialization and top of the stack clash probing loop, generating labels and comparison logic.\\n\\n- **`emit_stack_clash_protection_probe_loop_end()`** (line 2036): Emits the end of the probing loop with appropriate jump instructions.\\n\\nThese functions are declared in `gcc/explow.h` (lines 73-87).\\n\\n#### 2. **Target Hook Definition (gcc/target.def)**\\nThe generic stack clash mechanism is extended via the target hook `TARGET_STACK_CLASH_PROTECTION_ALLOCA_PROBE_RANGE` (lines 6534-6545). This hook allows targets to define an ABI-specific probing interval that may differ from the generic implementation.\\n\\n#### 3. **Default Target Hook Implementation (gcc/targhooks.cc)**\\nThe default implementation of `default_stack_clash_protection_alloca_probe_range()` is defined at line 2746, returning 0 (no target-specific probing range).
